## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(P) = 0.845(-1 + P/5.115)(1 - P/34.44)P + 0.845(1 - e^{-0.0969P})P$$

Let me expand the first term:
$$(-1 + P/5.115)(1 - P/34.44) = -1 + P/34.44 + P/5.115 - P^2/(5.115 \times 34.44)$$

So the first part becomes:
$$0.845P\left(-1 + P/34.44 + P/5.115 - P^2/176.16\right)$$
$$= 0.845(-P + P^2/34.44 + P^2/5.115 - P^3/176.16)$$

The second part:
$$0.845(P - Pe^{-0.0969P})$$

Combining:
$$f(P) = 0.845\left(-P + P^2(1/34.44 + 1/5.115) - P^3/176.16 + P - Pe^{-0.0969P}\right)$$

The $-P$ and $+P$ cancel:
$$f(P) = 0.845\left(P^2(0.02904 + 0.19550) - P^3/176.16 - Pe^{-0.0969P}\right)$$

$$f(P) = 0.845 \times 0.22454 \times P^2 - 0.845/176.16 \times P^3 - 0.845 \times P \times e^{-0.0969P}$$

So: $f(P) = aP^2 + bP^3 + cPe^{dP}$ where $a, b, c, d$ are specific constants, and notably $d < 0$.

**Key structure: $f(P) = \alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \gamma P e^{\delta P}$** (a cubic polynomial in P plus an exponential term $Pe^{\delta P}$, with NO constant term, NO linear P term, and NO dependence on $t$).

Wait, let me recheck. The $-P + P$ cancellation gives no linear term. Let me verify:
- First part gives: $0.845(-P + 0.2245P^2 - P^3/176.16)$
- Second part gives: $0.845(P - Pe^{-0.0969P})$
- Sum: $0.845(0.2245P^2 - P^3/176.16 - Pe^{-0.0969P})$

So $f(P) = \alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \gamma P e^{\delta P}$ with no constant, no linear term, no $t$ dependence.

The essential basis functions are: **$P^3$, $P^2$, $Pe^{\delta P}$** (where $\delta < 0$).

Now let me check each candidate:

### Candidate 1: $Pc_0 + Pc_1 e^{Pc_2} + Pc_3 + c_4 + c_5|Pc_6|$
Simplifies to: $(c_0+c_3)P + c_1 P e^{c_2 P} + c_4 + |c_5 c_6| |P|$
With $P \geq 0$: $= (c_0+c_3+|c_5c_6|)P + c_1 Pe^{c_2 P} + c_4$
This gives $aP + bPe^{cP} + d$. Missing $P^2$ and $P^3$. We need the linear and constant terms to be zero, but GT has no linear term. However, we can set $c_0+c_3+|c_5c_6| = 0$ and $c_4 = 0$. But $|c_5c_6| \geq 0$, so we'd need $c_0+c_3 \leq 0$. That's fine. But then we only have $Pe^{cP}$, missing $P^2$ and $P^3$.
**Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 2: $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2)P^2 + c_3P + c_4 + c_5\max(0,P+c_6) + c_7\max(0,P+c_8)$
For $P \geq 0$ and choosing $c_6, c_8 \geq 0$: $\max(0,P+c_6) = P+c_6$, giving polynomial terms. This becomes $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2)P^2 + (c_3+c_5+c_7)P + (c_4+c_5c_6+c_7c_8)$. This is a cubic polynomial - missing the exponential term.
**Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 3: $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2)P^2 + c_3P + c_4 + c_5\max(0,P+c_6)$
Similar to Candidate 2, just a cubic polynomial.
**Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 4: $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2+c_3)P^2 + (c_4+c_5)P + c_6 + c_7\log(c_8 e^{c_9 P}+1)$
The $\log(c_8 e^{c_9 P}+1)$ is a softplus-like function. This is NOT equivalent to $Pe^{\delta P}$. The softplus approaches $c_9P + \log c_8$ for large $P$ and $\log(c_8+1)$ for $P \to 0$. It cannot produce the $Pe^{\delta P}$ behavior.
**Candidate 4 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 5: $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2)P^2 + (c_3+c_4)P + c_5 + c_6\max(0,P+c_7)$
Cubic polynomial. Missing exponential.
**Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 6: $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2+c_3)P^2 + (c_4+c_5)P + c_6 + c_7\max(0,P+c_8)$
Cubic polynomial. Missing exponential.
**Candidate 6 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 7: $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2)P^2 + (c_3+c_4)P$
Cubic polynomial. Missing exponential.
**Candidate 7 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 8: $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2)P^2 + c_3P + c_4 + c_5|c_6P+c_7|$
For $P \geq 0$, if $c_6 > 0, c_7 > 0$: $|c_6P+c_7| = c_6P+c_7$. This is a cubic polynomial. Missing exponential.
**Candidate 8 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 9: $(c_0+c_3)P + c_1Pe^{c_2P} + c_4 + c_5\max(0,P+c_6)$
For $P \geq 0$ with $c_6 \geq 0$: $(c_0+c_3+c_5)P + c_1Pe^{c_2P} + c_4+c_5c_6$. Linear + exponential. Missing $P^2, P^3$.
**Candidate 9 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 10: $(c_0+c_3)P + c_1Pe^{c_2P} + c_4 + c_5\log(c_6P+1)\log(c_7t+1)$
Has $t$ dependence through $\log(c_7t+1)$. Setting $c_5=0$ removes it, leaving linear + exponential. Missing $P^2, P^3$.
**Candidate 10 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 11: $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2)P^2 + c_3P + c_4 + c_5e^{c_6P}$
This has $P^3, P^2, P, 1, e^{cP}$. GT has $P^3, P^2, Pe^{\delta P}$. The exponential here is $e^{cP}$, not $Pe^{cP}$. These are different basis functions. Can we get $Pe^{\delta P}$ from $e^{cP}$? No, they're linearly independent.
**Candidate 11 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 12: $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2+c_3)P^2 + (c_4+c_5)P + c_6P/(P+c_7) + c_8$
$P/(P+c_7)$ is a rational function, not exponential. Missing $Pe^{\delta P}$.
**Candidate 12 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 13: $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2+c_3)P^2 + (c_4+c_5)P + c_6$
Cubic polynomial. Missing exponential.
**Candidate 13 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 14: $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2)P^2 + c_3Pe^{c_4P} + c_5P + c_6$
This has $P^3, P^2, Pe^{c_4P}, P, 1$. GT is $\alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \gamma Pe^{\delta P}$. Setting $c_5 = 0, c_6 = 0$, we get $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2)P^2 + c_3Pe^{c_4P}$. This matches the GT structure! We need:
- $c_0 = -0.845/176.16 \approx -0.004797$
- $c_1+c_2 = 0.845 \times 0.22454 \approx 0.18974$
- $c_3 = -0.845$
- $c_4 = -0.0969$

Yes, this works!
**Candidate 14 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 15: $c_0P^2 + (c_1+c_4+c_5)P + c_2Pe^{c_3P}$
This is $aP^2 + bP + cPe^{dP}$. Missing $P^3$.
**Candidate 15 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 16: $c_0P^3 + c_1P^2 + c_2P + c_3/t^5 + c_4$
Has $t$ dependence. Setting $c_3=0$: cubic polynomial. Missing exponential.
**Candidate 16 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 17: $c_0P^6 + c_1P^3 + (c_2+c_3)P^2 + (c_4+c_5+c_6)P + c_7e^{c_8t} + c_9$
Has $P^6$ (set $c_0=0$), $t$ dependence (set $c_7=0$). Left with cubic polynomial. Missing exponential in $P$.
**Candidate 17 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 18: $c_0P^3 + c_1P^2 + c_2P + c_3$
Cubic polynomial. Missing exponential.
**Candidate 18 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 19: $c_0P\log(c_1P+1) + c_3P^{c_2}\log(c_4P+1) + c_5 + c_6e^{c_7P}$
Has $P\log(P+1)$ type terms and $e^{cP}$ (not $Pe^{cP}$). These basis functions don't match GT.
**Candidate 19 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 20: $(c_0+c_3)P + c_1Pe^{c_2P} + c_4$
Linear + $Pe^{cP}$ + constant. Missing $P^2, P^3$.
**Candidate 20 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 21: $c_0P^2 + c_1Pe^{c_2P} + c_3P + c_4P\max(0,P+c_5)$
For $P \geq 0$ with $c_5 \geq 0$: $c_4P(P+c_5) = c_4P^2 + c_4c_5P$. So: $(c_0+c_4)P^2 + c_1Pe^{c_2P} + (c_3+c_4c_5)P$. Missing $P^3$.

But wait - what if $c_5 < 0$? Then for $P < -c_5$: $\max(0, P+c_5) = 0$, and for $P \geq -c_5$: $\max(0, P+c_5) = P+c_5$. This creates a piecewise function, not a smooth $P^3$. Cannot match.
**Candidate 21 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 22: $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2)P^2 + c_3P$
Cubic polynomial. Missing exponential.
**Candidate 22 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 23: $c_0P^2e^{c_1t} + c_2P^2 + (c_3+c_4)P + c_5t^{c_6} + c_7$
Has $t$ dependence. Setting $c_0=0, c_5=0$: $c_2P^2 + (c_3+c_4)P + c_7$. Missing $P^3$ and exponential.
**Candidate 23 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 24: $c_1PP^{c_0} + c_2P + c_3P\max(0,-P+c_4) + c_5t^{c_6} + c_7$
$PP^{c_0} = P^{1+c_0}$. Has $t$ dependence (set $c_5=0$). Then $c_1P^{1+c_0} + c_2P + c_3P\max(0,-P+c_4)$. The max term is piecewise. Cannot produce $Pe^{\delta P}$.
**Candidate 24 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 25: $c_1P^{1+c_0} + c_2P + c_3P\max(0,P+c_4) + c_5t^{c_6} + c_7$
Similar issues. Set $c_5=0$. Piecewise polynomial. Cannot match exponential.
**Candidate 25 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 26: $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2)P^2 + c_3P + c_4$
Cubic polynomial. Missing exponential.
**Candidate 26 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 27: $c_0P^3 + c_1P^2 + c_2P + c_3t^{c_4} + c_5$
Has $t$ dependence. Setting $c_3=0$: cubic polynomial. Missing exponential.
**Candidate 27 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 28: $c_0P^2 + c_1P + c_2Pe^{c_3t}$
Has $t$ dependence. $c_2Pe^{c_3t}$ depends on $t$, not $P$ in the exponent. Setting $c_3=0$: $c_0P^2 + (c_1+c_2)P$. Missing $P^3$ and $Pe^{\delta P}$.
**Candidate 28 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 29: $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2+c_3)P^2 + (c_4+c_5+c_6)P + c_7$
Cubic polynomial. Missing exponential.
**Candidate 29 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 30: $c_0P^2 + c_1P/(c_2P+1) + c_3P + c_4|P| + c_5$
For $P \geq 0$: $c_0P^2 + c_1P/(c_2P+1) + (c_3+c_4)P + c_5$. Rational function, not exponential. Missing $P^3$ and $Pe^{\delta P}$.
**Candidate 30 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 31: $(c_0+c_3)P + c_1Pe^{c_2P} + c_4 + c_5\log(c_6e^{c_7P}+1)$
The softplus $\log(c_6e^{c_7P}+1)$ is not equivalent to $P^2$ or $P^3$. Missing polynomial terms.
**Candidate 31 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 32: $(c_0+c_1)P^2 + c_2Pe^{c_3P} + (c_4+c_7+c_8)P + c_5P\max(0,-P+c_6) + c_9$
For $P \geq 0$: if $c_6 > 0$, then for $P < c_6$: $c_5P(c_6-P) = c_5c_6P - c_5P^2$, and for $P \geq c_6$: 0. This is piecewise, cannot match smooth $P^3$.
**Candidate 32 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 33: $c_0P\log(c_1|P|+1) + c_2P + c_3Pe^{c_4|P|} + c_5$
For $P \geq 0$: $c_0P\log(c_1P+1) + c_2P + c_3Pe^{c_4P} + c_5$. Has $Pe^{c_4P}$ but also $P\log(c_1P+1)$. The $P\log$ term cannot produce $P^2$ and $P^3$ simultaneously. These are different basis functions.
**Candidate 33 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 34: $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2+c_3+c_4)P^2 + (c_5+c_6+c_7)P + c_8$
Cubic polynomial. Missing exponential.
**Candidate 34 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 35: $c_0P^2 + c_1P + c_2t^{c_3} + c_4$
Has $t$ dependence. Setting $c_2=0$: quadratic. Missing $P^3$ and exponential.
**Candidate 35 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 36: $c_0P^2e^{c_1t} + c_2P|P|^{c_3} + (c_4+c_5)P + c_6$
Has $t$ dependence. Setting $c_0=0$ (or $c_1=0$): For $P \geq 0$: $c_0P^2 + c_2P^{1+c_3} + (c_4+c_5)P + c_6$. Power law, not exponential in $P$.
**Candidate 36 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 37: $c_0P/(c_1P+1) + c_2P + c_3Pe^{c_4t}$
Has $t$ dependence in exponential. Setting $c_4=0$: $c_0P/(c_1P+1) + (c_2+c_3)P$. Rational + linear. Missing $P^2, P^3, Pe^{\delta P}$.
**Candidate 37 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 38: $(c_0+c_1)P^2 + c_2P/(c_3P+1) + c_4P + c_5|P| + c_6$
For $P \geq 0$: $(c_0+c_1)P^2 + c_2P/(c_3P+1) + (c_4+c_5)P + c_6$. Rational function. Missing $P^3$ and exponential.
**Candidate 38 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 39: $c_0P^3 + (c_1+c_2)P^2 + c_3P + c_4 + c_5\max(0,P+c_6) + c_7\log(c_8\log(c_9|P|+1)+1)$
Complex nested log. Cannot produce $Pe^{\delta P}$.
**Candidate 39 verdict: [NO MATCH]**

### Candidate 40: $c_0P^2 + c_1P/(c_2P+1) + c_3P + c_4P\sin(c_5t+c_6) + c_7|P| + c_8$
